25:T2ca5,<entryFree id="n28725" key="عَرَفَهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">عَرَفَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, O, Msb, K, &amp;c.,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">عَرِفَ</orth>
                  </form>, (O, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مَعْرِفَةٌ</foreign> (S, O, K) and <foreign lang="ar">عِرْفَانٌ</foreign> (S, O, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">عِرِفَّانٌ</foreign> (K) and <foreign lang="ar">عِرْفَةٌ</foreign>, (Msb, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">مَعْرِفَةٌ</foreign> is a simple subst., (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">He knew it; he had cognition of it;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, acquainted with it;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">عَلِمَهُ</foreign>: (K:) or <hi rend="ital">he knew it</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">عَلِمَهُ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">by means of any of the five senses;</hi> (Msb;) [and also, <hi rend="ital">by mental perception:</hi>] Er-Rághib says, <foreign lang="ar">المَعْرِفَةُ</foreign> is <hi rend="ital">the perceiving</hi> a thing <hi rend="ital">by reflection,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">by consideration of the effect</hi> thereof [<hi rend="ital">upon the mind</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sense</hi>], so that it has a more special meaning than <foreign lang="ar">العِلْمُ</foreign>, and its contr. is <foreign lang="ar">الإِنْكَارُ</foreign>; and one says, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَعْرِفُ ٱللّٰهَ وَرَسُولَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Such a one knows God and his apostle</hi>], but one does not say <foreign lang="ar">يَعْلَمُ ٱللّٰهَ</foreign>, making the verb [thus] to have a single objective complement, since man's <foreign lang="ar">مَعْرِفَة</foreign> [or knowledge] of God is [the result of] the consideration of his effects, without the perception of his essence; and one says, <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُ يَعْلَمُ كَذَا</foreign>, but not <foreign lang="ar">يَعْرِفُ كذا</foreign>, since <foreign lang="ar">المَعْرِفَةُ</foreign> is used in relation to <foreign lang="ar">عِلْم</foreign> [or knowledge] which is defective, to which one attains by reflection: it is from <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفْتُهُ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">I found,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">experienced, its</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَرْف</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">odour;</hi> or as meaning <hi rend="ital">I attained its</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عُرْف</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">limit:</hi> (TA:) it is said in the B that <foreign lang="ar">المَعْرِفَةُ</foreign> differs from <foreign lang="ar">العِلْمُ</foreign>, in meaning, in several ways: the former concerns the thing itself [which is its object;] whereas the latter concerns the states, or conditions, or qualities, thereof: also the former generally denotes <hi rend="ital">the perceiving</hi> a thing <hi rend="ital">as a thing that has been absent from the mind,</hi> thus differing from the latter; therefore the contr. of the former is <foreign lang="ar">الإِنْكَارُ</foreign>, and the contr. of the latter is <foreign lang="ar">الجَهْلُ</foreign>; and the former is <hi rend="ital">the knowing</hi> a thing itself <hi rend="ital">as distinguished from other things;</hi> whereas the latter concerns a thing collectively with other things: (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">علم</foreign>:) and sometimes they put   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28725-1" target="اعترف" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> in the place of <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَ</foreign>; (S, O;) [i. e.] <foreign lang="ar">اعترف الشَّىْءَ</foreign> signifies <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَهُ</foreign>: (Mgh, K:) and so, sometimes, does   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28725-2" target="استعرفُه" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (Har p. 486.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَ</foreign> is also used in the place of <foreign lang="ar">اعترف</foreign> [in the first of the senses assigned to the latter below]. (S, O.) See the latter verb, in four places.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَهُ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">He requited him.</hi> (O, K.) Ks read, (O, K,) and so five others, (Az, TA,) in the Kur [lxvi. 3], (O,) <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَعْضَهُ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">He requited</hi> her, namely, Hafsah, <hi rend="ital">for part</hi> [<hi rend="ital">thereof,</hi> i. e.] of what she had done: (Fr, O, K:) and he did so indeed by divorcing her: (Fr, TA:) or it means <hi rend="ital">he acknowledged part thereof:</hi> (K:) but others read <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28725-3" target="عَرَّفَ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بَعْضَهُ</foreign>, which, likewise, has the former of the two meanings expl. above: (Bd:) or this means <hi rend="ital">he told</hi> Hafsah <hi rend="ital">part thereof.</hi> (Fr, O, Bd, * TA. [See also 2.]) As first expl. above, this phrase is like the saying to him who does good or who does evil, <foreign lang="ar">أَنَا أَعْرِفُ لأَهْلِ الإِحْسَانِ وَأَعْرِفُ لِأَهْلِ الإِسَآءَةِ</foreign>, (O,) or <foreign lang="ar">لِلْمُحْسِنِ وَالمُسِىْءِ</foreign>, (K,) [<hi rend="ital">I know how to requite the doer of good and the doer of evil,</hi>] i. e. the case of the doer of good and that of the doer of evil are not hidden from me nor is the suitable requital of him. (O, K.) <foreign lang="ar">لَأَعْرِفَنَّكَهَا عَنْدَ رَسُولِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> occurs in a trad., meaning <hi rend="ital">I will assuredly requite thee for it in the presence of the Apostle of God so that he shall know thy evil-doing:</hi> and is used in threatening. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَ الفَرَسَ</foreign>, (S, O, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">عَرِفَ</orth>
                  </form>, (O,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَرْفٌ</foreign>, (O, K,) <hi rend="ital">He clipped the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عُرْف</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">mane</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of the horse.</hi> (S, O, K.)       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفْتُ عَلَى القَوْمِ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">عَرُفَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عِرَافَةٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">I was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became,</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَرِيف</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">over the people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">party;</hi> i. e., <hi rend="ital">manager,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">orderer, of their affairs;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar">عَرُفْتُ عَلَيْهِمْ</foreign>: (Msb:) or <foreign lang="ar">عَرُفَ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عَرَاعَةٌ</foreign>, signifies <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, an</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَرِيف</foreign>; (S, O, K;) as also <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">عَرِفَ</orth>
                  </form>; (K;) i. e., <hi rend="ital">a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَقِيب</foreign>: (S, O:) and when you mean that he acted as an <foreign lang="ar">عَرِيف</foreign>, you say, <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَ عَلَيْنَا سِنِينَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">عَرُفَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">عِرَافَةٌ</foreign>, [<hi rend="ital">he acted over us as an</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عريف</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">during some years,</hi>] like <foreign lang="ar">كَتَبَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَكْتُبُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">كِتَابَةٌ</foreign>. (S, O, K. *)       <sense type="A" n="4">-A4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَ لِلْأَمْرِ</foreign>, aor.     
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">عَرِفَ</orth>
                  </form>, <hi rend="ital">He was patient in relation to the affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">event;</hi> (K;) as also

                  <hi rend="ital">An odour,</hi> whether <hi rend="ital">fragrant</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fetid,</hi> (S, O, K, TA,) in most instances the former, (K, TA,) as when it is used in relation to Paradise: (TA:) and

                  <foreign lang="ar">عَرْفَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">How fragrant is its odour!</hi>]. (S, O.) And <foreign lang="ar">لَا يَعْجِزُ مَسْكُ السَّوْءِ عَنْ عَرْفِ السَّوْءِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The bad hide will not lack the fetid odour</hi>]; (S, O, K;) a prov.; (S, O;) applied to the low, ignoble, mean, or sordid, who will not cease from his evil doing; he being likened to the hide that is not fit for being tanned; (O, K;) wherefore it is cast aside, and becomes fetid.                   <hi rend="ital">The place</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">mountain</hi>] <hi rend="ital">where the pilgrims halt</hi> (Mgh, O, Msb, K) <hi rend="ital">on the day of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَة</foreign> [above mentioned], (O, K,) [described by Burckhardt as a granite hill, about a mile, or a mile and a half, in circuit, with sloping sides, rising nearly two hundred feet above the level of the adjacent plain,] <hi rend="ital">said to be nine miles,</hi> (Msb,) or <hi rend="ital">twelve miles,</hi> (K,) <hi rend="ital">from Mekkeh;</hi> (Msb, K;) said by J to be <hi rend="ital">a place in,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at, Minè,</hi> but incorrectly, (K, TA,) unless thereby be meant <hi rend="ital">near Minè;</hi> (TA;) also called by some   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28741-1" target="عَرَفَةُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (Mgh, Msb;) but the saying <foreign lang="ar">نَزَلْنَا عَرَفَةَ</foreign>, (S, O, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">نَزَلْتُ بِعَرَفَةَ</foreign>, (Msb,) [<hi rend="ital">We,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I, alighted at</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَة</foreign>,] is like a post-classical phrase, (S, O, K,) and (S, O) it is said to be (Msb) not genuine Arabic: (S, O, Msb:) <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَاتٌ</foreign> is a [proper] name in the pl. form, and therefore is not itself pluralized: (S, O, K:) it is as though the term <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَةٌ</foreign> applied to every distinct portion thereof: (TA:) as Fr says, it has, correctly, no sing.; (S, O;) and it is determinate as denoting a particular place; (Sb, S, O, K, TA;) and therefore not admitting the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>; (Sb, TA;) differing from <foreign lang="ar">الزَّيْدُونَ</foreign> [because this is a proper name common to a number of persons]: you say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰؤُلَآءِ عَرَفَاتٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَسَنَةً</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">These are 'Arafát, in a good state</hi>], putting the epithet in the accus. case because it is indeterminate [as a denotative of state, like <foreign lang="ar">مُصَدِّقًا</foreign> in the saying <foreign lang="ar">وَهُوَ الحَقُّ مُصَدِّقًا لِمَا مَعَهُمْ</foreign>, in the Kur ii. 85]: (S, O:) it is decl. (<foreign lang="ar">مَصْرُوفَةٌ</foreign> [more properly <foreign lang="ar">مُعْرَبَةٌ</foreign>]) because the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> is equivalent to the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">مُسْلِمِينَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مُسْلِمُونَ</foreign>, (S, O, K,) the tenween becoming equivalent to the <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign>, therefore, being used as a proper name, it is left in its original state, like as is <foreign lang="ar">مُسْلِمُونَ</foreign> when used as a proper name: (Akh, S, O, K:) [i. e.,] it is decl. in the manner of <foreign lang="ar">مُسْلِمَاتٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مُؤْمِنَاتٌ</foreign>, the tenween being like that which corresponds to the masc. pl. termination <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign>, not the tenween of perfect declinability, because it is a proper name and of the fem. gender, wherefore it does not admit the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>. (Msb.) <foreign lang="ar">عَرَفَاتٌ</foreign> was thus named because Adam and Eve knew each other (<foreign lang="ar">تَعَارَفَا</foreign>) there (IF, O, K, TA) after their descent from Paradise: (TA:) or because Gabriel, when he taught Abraham the rites and ceremonies of the pilgrimage, said to him “ Hast thou known? ” (<foreign lang="ar">أَعَرَفْتَ</foreign>), (O, K,) and he replied “ I have known ” (<foreign lang="ar">عَرَفْتُ</foreign>): (K:) or because it is a place sanctified and magnified, as though it were rendered fragrant (<foreign lang="ar">عُرِّفَ</foreign> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">طُيِّبَ</foreign>): (O, K:) or because the people know one another (<foreign lang="ar">يَتَعَارَفُونَ</foreign>) there: or, accord. to Er-Rághib, because of men's making themselves known (<foreign lang="ar">نِتَعَرُّفِ العِبَادِ</foreign>) there by religious services and prayers.
